Also, don&#x27;t even get close to a mole.   OUCH!  I still use that head on my legs, but have gone to the \\&quot;beginner\\&quot; head with rollers for underarms with no problems.     <li> I&#x27;d never used an epilator before, nor had I ever waxed my legs or underarms. But I really got sick of shaving constantly and dealing with stubble and cutting my ankles, etc etc etc, so I thought I&#x27;d give this a try. I listened to the advice of other reviewers and it helped a lot! So I&#x27;m passing on their advice and a few tips of my own:    1) Use Veet or Nair for a good two or three weeks before your first epi use. I found it softened my hair and made it easier. I still use Veet every now and again to wipe away lighter thigh hair and thinner leg hairs. Can&#x27;t believe how great it works after using the epi for two years! (Veet works much better if you first dampen your legs with a hot washcloth to open the hair follicles and soften the hair.)    2) Enjoy a glass of wine (or two) for the first epi. It does hurt, but just remember it will never hurt as bad again on your legs.     3) After two years, I barely even feel it on my legs. And the hair is WAY finer, comes in slower and lighter. Even with longish hair on my legs, you can barely see it or feel it...and I&#x27;m a brunette. I often do epi touch ups while watching tv. Remember, hair grows in cycles...a touchup every few days works great and goes faster than leaving it all for one hairy removal.    4) I use the epi on my underarms...it&#x27;s a little less painful after two years, but it still hurts (especially near my period). For underarms, make sure you stay dry or you&#x27;ll get a skin irritation! So apply deodorant or powder before using the epi on underarms. Much less irritation than shaving and hair comes in finer.    5) I tried to epi my bikini line and it was just too dang painful. Better luck to you!    6) For ingrown hairs on leg, I use a disinfected pin to lightly pop them out before using the epi.    7) I tried in grown hair serums and tea tree oil, etc., but eventually just stopped using them because they didn&#x27;t work for me. After two years of using the epi, I barely get irritation anymore anyway. But a helpful hint to avoid exacerbating any irritation, avoid putting on lotions or cremes for a while after you epi.</li>
    <li> This is a great product...I use it as a supplement to waxing, for places that are harder to wax, and also for the little hairs that waxing sometimes misses.  The first time I used it was pretty painful, as other reviewers have also said.  After a couple times though, it is much more tolerable, less painful, less noticeable.  I use it every few days to clean up little hairs that are growing in at different rates, and my legs are nice and smooth now most of the time with little effort!    The only thing I would say against it is it is VERY noisy, so if you have housemates they will all know (or wonder) what you are doing.  HArd to be private with it.    Mostly I love it!</li>

    <li> It appears this product works extremely well for SOME hair/skin types.  BUT, if you&#x27;ve never epilated before I strongly urge you to begin with a small test patch first.  Thoroughly epilate one patch of one leg, perhaps just to the outside of the shin bone or wherever the hair grows thick.   Then shave everywhere else.  WAIT several weeks until you get re-growth on the test patch.  I didn&#x27;t think of doing this when I bought the Braun epilator.  I followed the package instructions and other reviewers&#x27; recommendations carefully to epilate both legs completely.  I did not find it at all painful, by the way.  I exfoliated often, and waited.  I encountered two problems.  1st, the machine did not successfully pull all the hair from the root.  Some hairs were broken at or near the surface, so I had a fair bit of &#x27;stubble&#x27; immediately.  I kept epilating until eventually all the hairs were &#x27;pulled&#x27;.  But that wasn&#x27;t the deal breaker.  After a couple of weeks I noticed a strange, mildly unpleasant tingling sensation on my legs.  After a few days of this I noticed that my legs were covered with hair.  The re-growth had come in.  The problem was that most of the hair was growing JUST UNDER a very thin layer of skin.  The hairs were completely visible but impossible to shave OR epilate, protected as they were under that thin layer.  I had to tweeze each hair (and there were many)  out from under the skin.  Once the hair was growing normally again, I decided to give the epilator another try.  I thought the problem might improve over time.  It didn&#x27;t.  After 3 full rounds with the same results,I stopped using the epilator several weeks ago and my legs still haven&#x27;t recovered. I&#x27;m still struggling to get rid of the cycle of ingrowns, and the unsightly red bumps some of them caused.  I think this problem probably occurs only for certain hair/skin types.  I strongly caution all new users to test a small patch to see how the epilator works for your hair/skin.</li>

    <li> I absolutely love this product for my legs. I have very thick, coarse hair. The tweezers, rather than being two metal thingies that clamp together (as with the 20 tweezer silk epil), are actually just one metal hicky that clamps against the plastic of the epilator head.  It works fine, but I have to wonder about the long term reliability of such a design and wonder why Braun would make it like this.    Then, the epilator head is designed so that, if you don&#x27;t have the massaging head on it (an attachment I find useless and cumbersome) the gears of the head are exposed, which is,of course, an aesthetic matter, but makes the quality of this product seem less than that of the other silk epils.    The light, which seems like a good idea, is really just kind of...  blinding.It does illuminate the area being epilated, but it does so at the cost of seeing anything else clearly.  It has that effect where, you know, if you look at just a little bit of a picture, you can&#x27;t figure out what the whole picture is?  It would be easier to see all your legs in good light than try to see a small portion at a time in great light.  Plus if you are moving the epilator in such a fashion that the light is on the other side...  IE you are doing the back of your left calve, from the inside, sitting on the floor and moving the epilator sort of down and around to the back...  you really can&#x27;t figure out what you are looking at.  It&#x27;s hard to describe, but the light makes things harder to figure out, not easier - and there is no way to disable the light.    I have actually taken the 40 tweezer head and use it on my other silk epil, because I really don&#x27;t like the light.  I use it in the broadest diaylight I can, finding early morning light as the sun comes in our patio door to be especially helpful/horrifying (you are always hairier than you think you are).  I think if I had to use the light, if I didn&#x27;t have the option to use the lightless unit, I would be a lot more unhappy with this product.    Anyway it&#x27;s great in ways but...  I am left somehow thinking \\&quot;Wow, Braun had a great idea here!\\&quot; and \\&quot;What the $@%! was Braun thinking here??\\&quot; which is kind of odd.  They should really just take the 20 tweezer unit and make it have 40 double-metal-thingied tweezers, don&#x27;t change anything else.      OK, the blue sparklies are nice.    This is actually sort of a Eurpopean product - if you go to Braun&#x27;s website, they only have the X&#x27;Elle on the European site.  I wonder if this model of the X&#x27;Elle (there are several other models with various attachments) is a US - only model and is of lesser quality than the others.  No way to know for sure but I find it odd that this is the only one for sale in the US (at this time) and the quality is so not in keeping with the other Silk Epils.    I am really not sure of giving this 3 or 4 stars...  so I will err on the side of generous here.  It&#x27;s not a bad product, but bear in mind its flaws.</li>

    <li> For reference: I&#x27;d traditionally have to shave once a day to once every other day and I&#x27;d never had experience with epilation or waxing.  I have owned this product for almost a month.    First off, what it WON&#x27;T do:  1) It will not give you silky smooth legs to the touch.  2) It won&#x27;t get every hair every time, and it may miss finer hairs completely.  3) It won&#x27;t be like eating ice cream in the park (pain factor).  4) It will NOT last weeks.  5) It will not look nice immediately (need time for the redness/bumps to go down).    But it WILL:  1) It will give you VISIBLY nice legs for about a week at a time.  2) It will become more efficient as time goes on (first time ~3 hours, now ~0.5 hours) and it will dominate coarse, dark hair.  3) It will go from feeling like fire ants are devouring your legs to a vaguely uncomfortable sensation within a few uses.    As for the product itself:  1) The light is extremely useful for spotting finer or missed hairs.  2) It is comfortable to hold and feels solid, plus the kit is nice--I like that it came with a little brush to clean it.    I would recommend:  1) A pumice stone, loofah, etc. to exfoliate--some ingrown hair is kind of inevitable with this thing, but I got those shaving, too.  2) Rubbing alcohol or witch hazel to clean the tweezers (and to prevent infected ingrown hairs, so far all mine are just caught growing along the surface but not \\&quot;impacted\\&quot; if you will).    3) Taking some advil before your first time.  I know some people are recommending an alcoholic drink, but booze tends to dilate blood vessels near the surface of the skin and (in my non-expert opinion) I can&#x27;t help but feel this&#x27;d be the same as taking two steps forward and one step back.  4) If you have a bigger bathroom, you may need an extension cord since you&#x27;ll probably want to do this over the tub to avoid a mess..    Final/qualitative remarks:  I haven&#x27;t worked up the chutzpah to use it on my bikini line or underarms (tried the latter once and it startedto bleed), but those take only a couple of minutes to shave in the first place... I mostly like being able to throw on shorts or a skirt without worrying about my legs.  Every time I&#x27;d get goosebumps after shaving, I could practically feel the hair growing and my legs would no longer be smooth.  Epilation eliminated this problem and I find it fantastically rewarding to see the hairs ripped out by the root (you can see the little bulb on the end, so it&#x27;s definitely not just ripping it off at the surface).  I also love the fact that this thing costs less than a single wax job around here; I&#x27;m very satisfied with my investment.  If you&#x27;ve got a reasonable pain tolerance (for the first one or two uses, especially) and you&#x27;re committed, you&#x27;ll probably love this thing as much as I do.  :)</li>

    <li> Product Usage:  Some reviews say that it didn&#x27;t hurt much at all. Other reviews say it hurt a fair bit during the first use. My first time use was very painful and it took quite a while for me to finish the first session. My second session was MUCH quicker and far less painful. Most of the time, I felt a mild plucking sensation as opposed to the \\&quot;OW!\\&quot; feeling I had during the first use. If you wax semi-often, it shouldn&#x27;t hurt much at all. This thing is basically controlled waxing. Sensitive areas of the body included ankles, wrists, elbows, and knees. If you&#x27;re one of those who find epilation painful on the first use, try setting it to the \\&quot;slow\\&quot; mode and twisting your wrist left and right as if you were making paint brush strokes. This will get hairs bit by bit while pulling the epilator back after it grabs a few, reducing the first-time pain from \\&quot;constant\\&quot; to \\&quot;semi-constant\\&quot;.    Women with smaller hands may find the unit a little akward to use, especially when getting the hard to reach spots like the back of a leg or arm. Also, I&#x27;ve never felt a pinching feeling when the epilator is pressed too close to the skin. Finally, redness will occur from use so I advise using it a full 24-48 hours BEFORE going somewhere important or when doing something in which you feel looks matter. Two days after use and still smooth skinned! I have seen many people suggest using a mild moisturizer though after epilation to soothe your skin.      The Smartlite:  Ingenious idea! It helps highlight the hairs in the area you&#x27;ve got the light near and can show you hair in places you might not have expected to see it in. Without this, I would never know if I had gotten all the hairs or not.      Product came with:  The epilator came with a \\&quot;beginner\\&quot; head that&#x27;s supposed to sooth the skin and lessen the feeling of pain through vibrations but I haven&#x27;t noticed a difference between either the beginner head or the precision head. It also came with a shaving head for the men afraid to try it on a particularly long haired area. The shaver also came with an attachment that combs the longer hair is \\&quot;certain areas\\&quot; into the trimmer, making for easy shaving/trimming. The trimmed hair doesn&#x27;t feel prickly or stabby-sharp like hair does a day after shaving.      Storage:  The product came with a durable feeling, draw-string pouch large enough to contain everything. Everything being the shaver head, various attachments, power cord, cleaner brush, and the epilator itself without feeling as if I were cramming the pouch overly full of things. So, storage is fairly easy.      Cons:  Occasionally, I had to turn the machine off to let the motor cool off in fear of it otherwise burning out during my first-time area use session because it was taking so long due to me being a wimp with pain. Second time use, I didn&#x27;t encounter this problem. Secondly, it is a bit noisy so I avoid using it late at night or before the average household bed time.      Overall, this is a good product and worth the money but I would still suggest people shop around for the best price. $50 USD+ is a LOT of money to pay for anything these days so make sure you get the best damned deal you can!</li>

To deal with ingrown hairs (A MUST TO READ!!): when you epilate, if you don&#x27;t do anything to your skin to prevent ingrown hairs, expect ALMOST EVERY hair to become ingrown! My hair is super thick and grows in very quickly, and I have to epilate at least a few days every week (versus others who can make it 3-4 weeks). I&#x27;ve been using a body brush for a month on my legs, and the results are just as good, if not better, than Prince Reigns. My skin is also super soft and feels buttery (boyfriend LOVES IT!), no in-grown hairs, and no more sticky, gooey legs. My skin can rock and still breathe! It&#x27;s better for you, natural, and way more cost-effective.    How to use body brush: Do it dry! Don&#x27;t get the bristles wet. Every day before you shower, brush down your body from chin to toe. The bristles are course and it&#x27;s another thing you get used to, but you&#x27;ll crave it after you start. Make sure you really go over the epilated areas well. The brush removes dead surface layers, improves circulation, and polishes and smooths the skin. Easy, takes about 3 minutes. If you love your skin and like feeling beautiful, also look into getting a Clarisonic Pro facial brush. Trust me, you&#x27;ll feel like a million bucks and look like it, too!</li>

    <li> I purchased this epilator to replace a much older Braun model in which the gears had begun to slip.  Considering the old one was nearly 15 years old, I would say that it held up quite well.  But this baby!  Wow, what a difference!  It is so much more gentle than the older model was, and the LED light feature illuminates even the finest of hairs. The shaver/trimmer attachment for the device is very nice, and does a wonderful job on the bikini line.     I&#x27;ve been using this method of hair removal for over 15 years and I&#x27;ve seen many posts that complain about \\&quot;stubble\\&quot;.  The stubble is a by-product of hairs that break off, rather than get pulled out, while using the epilation process.  For first time users, or if you haven&#x27;t used the product for a long time, this is very common.  First, the length of the hair is important.  If it&#x27;s too long, it will likely break off, especially if the machine only grabs the hair at the end.  However, if you use the shaver/trimmer head first, to cut the hairs to optimal length, it will greatly reduce the amount of breakage that occurs.  For the hairs that do break, simply allow a day or two for them to grow out a bit, and reuse the epilator to extract them.</li>

I tested it on a few friends, my fiancÃ©&#x27;s arm, and a few volunteer male legs and chests.  It works well on men because of the thickness of their hair (trimmed first). So the truth is, just like the latest \\&quot;Must HAVE Allure Magazine Beauty Product of the YEAR\\&quot;...one size just doesn&#x27;t fit all.  Sometimes, today&#x27;s \\&quot;best\\&quot; beauty product just is not your shade.  Sometimes, the latest clothing trend just isn&#x27;t the right cut for you.  And sometimes, the best epilator on the market just won&#x27;t leave you baby soft.     This product will be your best friend, if:    You have coarse or thick hair.    You have firm, tone, well-exfoliated skin in all of the areas intending to be epilated.      This will be your enemy, if:    You have fine hair, or soft blonde hair.  The hairs will be cut off, rather than epilated.    You have areas of thin skin, loose skin, dry skin, or skin that needs vigorous exfoliation.  (If you are prone to ingrown hairs, I am talking to you.) This product is likely to make you bleed and leave tiny red bloody spots.      With that in mind, this is absolutely worth trying out.  For those it works for, it&#x27;s an utter miracle machine.  And if it doesn&#x27;t work for you?  Well, at least you&#x27;ll stop having that burning, tingling, \\&quot;what if?\\&quot; anymore. My underarms - This area is a whole other story!!! The hair on my underarm is totally different from my leg hair. When I was shaving, I had to shave every single day. I have dark, coarse underarm hair (and I have a lot of it). 12 hours after shaving, I usually have a 5 o&#x27;clock shadow. Sometimes I would pluck my underarm hair and I always loved the results but it just took forever to do. When I discovered this epilator, it was a dream come true! Because I was so used to plucking my underarm hair, it didn&#x27;t hurt at all to use the epilator on this area! It takes about a couple runs over the same area to remove the hair. It takes about a minute or two to do both underarms. This is how I used it: First time, I let my underarm hair grow out for two days (it wasn&#x27;t a pretty sight!). I used the epilator and as I&#x27;ve mentioned already, it was not painful at all.  The next day when I took a shower, I accidently grabbed my shaver as a reflex (I&#x27;ve been shaving my underarm for like 15 years every single day)...then I realized that i didn&#x27;t have to shave anymore!!! On the third day, I noticed that some of the underarm hair had started to sprout already. By the fourth day, I had to use the epilator again. And that has been my pattern for the last 5 months...every 3-4 days I will use the epilator for my underarm. I have not shaved my underarms since I got this epilator. I&#x27;m loving the freedom of not shaving every day! Using this epilator hasn&#x27;t made my underarm hair any thinner like it did with my leg hair.     My Bikini area - I wax (myself) in this area. I have thick, coarse, dark hair in this area so shaving is not an option (unless I want to shave everyday...which I don&#x27;t want to do). I thought that it was pretty painful the first time I used the epilator even though I&#x27;m used to waxing my bikini area. I have not gotten the nerve to do a complete Brazilian bikini hair removal with this epilator (I&#x27;m not that brave...yet). I have to say that this does a good job in removing the hair...but I do end up with more ingrown hair than with waxing (which other reviewers have commented about). I guess with waxing, it removes the the dead outer layer of the skin so it does exfoliate the skin but with epilating, it just removes the hair so you have to remember to do extra exfoliating before and after using your epilator. I use Tend Skin to help prevent and treat ingrowns and I have to use it more frequently when using the epilator. I think I prefer waxing over epilating but in this case, epilating takes less time so I tend to epilate my bikini area. Unlike my legs, it is still relatively painful (not as painful as the first time) but I guess my skin is more sensitive in this area. I use the epilator maybe twice a month on my bikini area. I&#x27;m not so overly concerned about being hairless in this area.     Upper lips  - I used to wax once a week. My upper lip hair is relatively thin and sparse but I do have black hair. Epilation with Braun has completely replaced waxing. I tried [[ASIN:B0000DK5LW Emjoi AP-9L Epi Slim Cosmetic Hair Remover]] but it could not get the tiny, thin hair out. With this Braun epilator, it removes the tiniest hair, even the ones that are barely sprouting out of the skin. It takes about a minute or two to remove everything. I use the epilator once a week on this area and that&#x27;s all I need. I don&#x27;t get ingrowns (never have) on my upper lips.     As you can see, overall I have had a positive experience with this epilator and I totally recommend this to anyone! One annoying thing about this is that the cord gets tangled very easily...but that&#x27;s not super important. Maybe the next time I get an epilator, I might get the cordless ones but for now, I&#x27;m happy with this Braun epilator!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve had this epilator for 7 months now.  It&#x27;s been a wonderful thing for me, but not without its issues.  So here is my synopsis.  For reference, I&#x27;m a dark haired person with sensitive fair skin who has both been waxed by pros and done it herself for the last 10-15 years...  It&#x27;s a great little gadget that will keep you hairless and smooth - for me, I have to do a &#x27;touch up&#x27; approx 1x per week during bare leg season.  But my hair grows fast and coarse.  I can get away with a longer timeframe during the winter months since my hubbie never seems to notice if my legs are smooth and silky or if I&#x27;m a sasquach.  ;-)     #1.  Does it hurt?  Of course it does. You&#x27;re yanking out hairs by the root.  It&#x27;s probably a bit worse than waxing because you have to go over the same area a few times to catch all the hairs.  But if you can stand waxing, you can grit your teeth and stand this.  Or take an aspirin/advil/tylenol first to help a bit.    #2  Does it scar?  NO.  In my opinion, it will definitely cause ingrown hairs, but no actual scarring.  If you have an ingrown hair that becomes deeply embedded without being removed, it may leave a dark spot on the surface skin.  What has worked well for me is the following:      - Exfoliate both with a scrub wash regularly and use a chemical exfoliator (such as KP duty) once a week or so.  - Follow the product instructions and make sure to use rubbing alcohol to clean the exfoliator parts every time you use it.  - If you need to remove an ingrown hair, use good tweezers which are dipped in rubbing alcohol first.      What else.  I like the light.  Yes, it is noisy, but the motor works well so far, which is more important to me than quietness.  Does it break the hairs?  Yes, I&#x27;d say it breaks some hair rather than removing it, but not overly so.      Overall it functions as advertised. It takes about an hour for me to do both legs and bikini area properly each go.  A professional waxing is probably less painful and more effective/less ingrowns - so if that route is affordable to you, I&#x27;d say go for that.  But for someone who gets 5 o&#x27;clock shadow on her legs after shaving in the morning, and can&#x27;t standing paying $80+tip for waxing every couple of weeks, this is really a great product.  It&#x27;ll pay for itself the first time you use it!!  What do you have to lose?  Try it!!!</li>

I had initial trouble with ingrown hairs, but have found that exfoliating scrubs, like sugar scrubs and similar products, really help make a difference. In order to keep the progressively softer hairs from getting trapped below the skin&#x27;s surface, you have to help things along by scrubbing the area that you&#x27;re epilating with an exfoliant.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Additionally, Braun epilators DO remove the entire hair shaft, as opposed to just cutting at the skin&#x27;s surface layer, like razors do. I am not a waxer and while I occasionally plucked with tweezers, this is the first time I have removed hair by the roots a lot at a time.     The positives:   - The light! It was not a major selling point at the time I purchased it, but it is extremely handy. Even when I have the bathroom lights on, it can be hard to see the hairs on my legs (and I&#x27;m brunette) so this came in really handy.   - It&#x27;s not painful on the legs. Even the bikini line is tolerable, but after trying out my underarms, I know that I&#x27;ll just stick to my legs.   - It lasts about 1.5 weeks. I LOVE that I don&#x27;t have to shave every couple of days.     So even though I have a long list of negatives, I probably would still buy this (but just barely) for the price I paid of $58.43. I wish I knew if some of the cheaper epilators would have gotten the job done for less, but it&#x27;s too late for that now... so here is my list of negatives:     The negatives:   - It is very loud. I have two young kids and it is so loud that I would only consider epilating when they are not sleeping or taking naps.   - The massaging roller clip. To me it is awkward and doesn&#x27;t prevent any more pain than the efficiency clip.   - The shaver attachment. I am really disappointed with this one. Before I purchased this item, I justified my purchase by thinking that if I couldn&#x27;t handle epilating, at least I would have an electric shaver which I had been thinkingabout getting anyway. When I found that epilating my underarms was a little too painful for me, I tried using the shaver attachment. It doesn&#x27;t shave as quickly or effortlessly like I had hoped. In order to shave my underarms closely, I really had to press the shaver attachment onto the skin in quick, repetitive movements. It is SO much easier to just use a disposable razor for my underarms.   - Ingrown hairs. At first, I didn&#x27;t see any, but after 1.5 weeks, I started noticing that quite a few hairs were becoming ingrown. When I used to shave with a disposable razor, I never had this problem. In order to get the ingrown hairs out, I have had to break my skin and pluck them out. This then tends to leave a tiny scab that takes about a week to heal. This means that although my legs are mostly hairless, I have little scabs on them that make it look like I was attacked by mosquitos.   - The need to go over the same area more than once. I read the directions and held the epilator as it recommended, but I still find myself going over the same area usually at least twice. This doesn&#x27;t annoy me too much.   - I wish this was cordless. I knew it was corded, but realized that it would be so much nicer if this could be cordless with a rechargable battery. That would allow the flexibility of shaving wherever, and not necessarily where there is a power outlet.   - I also wish that there was a way of it storing the hair that it pulls out so that I could then clean the unit easily. Instead, the hairs it pulls out end up wherever -- the floor, my legs, or the unit itself.</li>

    <li> I think the other reviews have mostly covered the epilation side of this, but: It really isn&#x27;t as scary as it seems. The best way i can describe the sensation is this: When i was younger i would steal my father&#x27;s electric shaver to use on my legs, and since i didn&#x27;t know how to use it very well i would push it too hard into my skin in an effort to shave closer. I pushed it so hard that i could feel the blades on the other side of the grill nipping at my skin. That&#x27;s what epilating feels like.    I do have a few pain-management tips if you find that it&#x27;s too much:    1. Take some ibuprofen or naproxen 15 minutes before starting.    2. Stretch your skin taut, as far as it will go (don&#x27;t hurt yourself obviously). This is especially helpful around the calves.    3. (And this is the most important one!) Don&#x27;t be delicate! You will probably feel the urge to take quick little nips and then pull the epilator away -- don&#x27;t do this, it just makes it hurt more (plus it takes longer). It seems counter-intuitive, but keep it in contact with your skin the whole time. Do one little spot at a time, in tiny circular or back-and-forth motions, and when it&#x27;s completely finished move slowly to the next spot.    OK, aside from the actual act of epilating:    - The epilator feels fine in your hand. It seemed bigger in the picture to me than it really was, so if it looks really chunky to you too, don&#x27;t worry.    - It hasn&#x27;t got a battery, it will only run off the mains. The cable it comes with is probably long enough for most people, but if you&#x27;re like me and your tub is on the opposite side of the bath room from the wall socket (and you don&#x27;t want to get hair all over your floor), you might need ashort extension cord.    - Contrary to the other reviews, i have found the shaver attachment to be extremely poor. I am not a regular user of electric shavers, but i have tried a couple over the years, so i feel i have a basis for comparison. This one is just awful to the point of being useless. It will trim the hairs, eventually, so they&#x27;re short enough to epilate, but it will take AGES (it&#x27;d probably be faster to use cuticle scissors...). It will NOT get close enough to do the job of a normal shaver.    So if you&#x27;re thinking to yourself (as i was), &#x27;oh hey, this is a sure thing, even if i don&#x27;t like the epilator i&#x27;ll still have a perfectly good shaver!&#x27;, you should probably rethink it. If you can see the hair you waited too long to epilate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Epilate EVERY day!  You will always have hair growing, but after you pluck one out by the root it takes that individual hair about a week or two to grow back.  You will have other hairs appearing the next day after you use your epilator though.  It will take a couple of weeks of everyday use, but eventually all your hairs will be taking so long to grow back that you will have beautiful baby-bare skin.  ALSO - since shaving with a razor doesn&#x27;t take out the root, the hair you&#x27;ve had since puberty has had a Long time to set up shop in your skin - this means that the root is going to be fixated in place a lot better than hair that&#x27;s had to regrow after plucking.  This is why the first time users are going to have a lot more pain than the people that use it all the time.&lt;br /&gt;*the red bumps first time users have will also get less and less with each use&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. The problem with this method is that you won&#x27;t be able to get all the hairs this way, but if you start this way you will remove some hairs and your biggest goal is to have as few hairs at one time going through the epilator&#x27;s pluckers.  It doesn&#x27;t hurt at all if you&#x27;re plucking 1 hair, but it starts to feel pretty intense if there&#x27;s a ton going through it!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4. Epilate right after bath or shower - a body that&#x27;s just been steamed will let loose its hair follicles much easier than a dry, hard body.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. Even though I shaved myself nearly bald before epilating, the hair follicles in my groin were so firmly rooted it was torture to mass pluck them.  So, I plucked hairs one at a time with tweezers until I&#x27;d taken out over half the growth.  After that the epilating was a breeze, and now that the hair growing there is new and not so firmly in place, I can epilate them all without much pain.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6.     <li> This was my second epilator....I purchased a less expensive one (by Revlon) the first time around, since I wasn&#x27;t sure if I would prefer epilation over shaving. Well, I&#x27;m hooked! You&#x27;ll find that the hair that grows back is the soft, fine hair your legs once had, before you started shaving it and stimulating that tough, picky re-growth we all know and hate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Braun epilator is a great little machine, and it has some advantages over the cheaper model. The light really helps me to see the tricky little hairs that used to get away. The Braun unit also utilizes a different tweezer design than the cheaper model. On the Revlon model, both sides of the \\&quot;tweezers\\&quot; moved, opening and closing quickly to pluck out the hairs. On the Braun, one side of the \\&quot;tweezer\\&quot; is stationary and made of a tacky plastic that helps to lift fine hairs....only the other side moves to create the pinching action. Because of this design, the Braun does a better job of grabbing the hairs, especially the fine ones. I had to replace my Revlon unit when the epilator went to pieces. All in all, the Braun epilator just seems to be a more sturdy machine, and in my opinion the superior design, more efficient epilation and other features make it worth the higher price.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I love my little machine!     <li> PAIN:    The product description is very misleading. Using this is by no means &#x27;painless&#x27; nor does it feel like a &#x27;massage&#x27; where the rolllers &#x27;glide over the skin&#x27;. Don&#x27;t be gullible, ripping out hair from the roots cannot be such a pleasant and relaxing experience.    The level of pain depends on where you&#x27;re using this.. I had no problem doing the lower half of my legs/arms; the upper halves hurt a little more; underarms hurt quite a bit depending on how taut my skin was (tauter hurt less); and I will probably never try the bikini area again.    I&#x27;m sure it will hurt more/less depending on each person&#x27;s waxing/shaving history, on the thickness/fineness of the hair, and your level of tolerance for pain.     RESULTS:    Unless all of your hair grows at the exact same rate, you probably won&#x27;t have perfectly smooth skin for &#x27;up to 6 weeks&#x27; as claimed. However I&#x27;ve found that the porcupine/cactus-like feeling that comes with stubbles growing back after 3 days, is significantly reduced. Also, fair skinned people with dark hair don&#x27;t have to worry about the leftover roots showing through from under the skin after shaving. It&#x27;s an added value for people whose hair color is much darker than their skin&#x27;s.    You may have to do a quick shave or epilate or pluck for maintaining the near perfect hairless skin; straggler hairs are bound to appear for most people.
